< rate>
5</rate>
< review>
This is a large rural county park that is full of beautiful large oak trees. Antelope creek runs along the parks western boundary and provides and excellent spot to cool off. The park has many picnic tables and bar-b-que pits. There is a nice playground for the kids. There is also some horseshoe pits if you bring some horseshoes. The bathrooms have sinks and flushing toilets.
This is a beautiful park to spend the day with the family and also a good place to have large get togethers or birthday parties.
Leased pets are also welcomed which is a plus for me and my dogs!<//review>

The XLB were juicy and all in tact, but the pork and soup inside lacked some flavor. The complementing vinegar sauce was delicious, with pieces of shredded ginger. < pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM8vf8IMhVe9rr5l_a_rweLGGaug92TjjTTDKjH=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPlpJeHvrwvF41WzMJiVnJr7mn3OXaloXZy2Jaw=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM842Dw_TAAtuwat30y5P7zurklVfC50ihiyKGB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOqN-bv44ncRkX8cMorYD_UnDDIuTa-1YTuFB3f=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>
<Review>There are a lot of fun, cheap, easy crafts you can try, and they provide all the materials! I had fun painting rocks and enjoying a cider drink. Prices are fair; you can paint 1 rock for $2.

We're going back to try string art--be aware, they said the large size can take 3 hours! A few friends are going back for the wine bottle etching class. We were going to join, but will be out of state.

The layout is okay. The front has the bar and seating, including comfy chairs and sofas. There is an awesome giant mural on the wall. Then there's a narrow hallway with staff offices and past that it opens up to the large crafting room. It would be nice if these areas could be a little more integrated (I think that narrow hallway acts too much as a divider). I spent my time going between my friends in the front and friends in the back, but once I started crafting I stayed in that room, so then we were separated. I worry that people might come in the 'front' entrance (I think there's also an entrance from the Plaza to the crafts side) and get stuck at the bar area without venturing back to the crafts area, which would really be a shame. Maybe showcasing more of the crafts (including pricing and instructions) in the bar area would intrigue people to walk back. Also, making sure the bartenders know about the crafts would help since they are talking to the customers when they order. Maybe cross-training would help integrate the arts with the drafts.

Really relaxed vibe. A few hipsters, but overall it felt more laid back than 'ahh is this place too trendy for me?'. It's really cool that the owner's mom is visiting from the Midwest to help out her daughter. We were there on International Women's Day and she helped cheer on the girl power vibe.< /Review>< Response>
None< /Response>

<Text>Panda is consistent if nothing else. The food is good enough so the rating is high. I do have a complaint though. This has to be the only fast food place that will not let you change or special order anything. If you are a vegetarian then you honestly might as well skip panda. Every single main entree has meat in it. Your options are rice, noodles and greens. All three are sides. They have an incredible stock of fresh veggies in the cooler but will not make anything that is not on the menu. Even though there are locations that have had a vegetarian option, including this one. They still will not make a veggie dish special order for you. I have asked enough times to know not to bother. I am personally not vegetarian, but my wife is vegan. Regardless that is two customers that would frequent this place and have in the past but honestly don't bother much anymore.

I want to reiterate, I can go to any other fast food place and they will make me anything they have in the kitchen without hesitation just to take my money. Once done with that, I received an email from Zack Bilbrey, (Internet Sales Manager) informing me of some purchasing options, and assuring me that I would be able to work with Chris.  Once I get to the dealership, both Chris and Zack greet me and reassure that a favorable deal will get done.  Midway through the process, I am introduced to Nick Dubiel (General Sales Manager). In accordance with the others, Nick made sure that I was able to get a good deal with low interest and reasonable payments.  He was friendly, attentive, and was committed to go out of his way to accommodate.  Lastly there was Eric ZuWalick, the Finance Manager.  Probably the most reassuring things about Eric was the fact that he was clear in his communication with me and he made me completely aware of all extended protection options that were available to me.  He took his time explaining everything to me and answered all of my questions.

I understand this a bit of a lengthy read, but these 4 completely deserve it.  I expect this kind of service from an individual when I make significant purchases like this, but to see everyone try so hard for me and for them all to be on the same page like that is truly unique.  I felt like I've known them all for years.  With that said, whatever you guys are doing over at Mossy Nissan Escondido, keep it up!  I've been apart of a few car purchases, but none of them stack to up to this experience.

Again, thank you (a lot!)

Sincerely,
